Ford Dental is amazing. My experience here is second to none. I neglected my teeth for almost 4 years before visiting. Backpacker from Europe here. I got a recommendation from some locals in Sonora to come here. It was already very late when I arrived to this RV park and I had no place to stay, so I really didn't think it's a crime to pitch a tent in RV park. At 7 am got wakened up by crappy looking guy, who threatened to call police if I don't leave immediately. I explained I had no bad intentions and offered to pay for a stay with no respond. Maybe I was wrong, maybe didn't know rules or regulations, but this felt a bit of overkill at least.My late arrival to this place was not planed as it happened because I had to cancel my hiking trip from Lake Tahoe to Yosemite due to snow conditions in High Sierras. Luckily, I met plenty of nice people on my way, who gave me rides to come back to San Francisco as there was no public transportation in Sonora area. < review>
Took one of my cars in for an oil change because I got lazy and didn't want to do it myself at that moment. We were the only car in at the time and it took a while, but part of that is they had to jump the battery which the car DID have a bad battery. They DID NOT try to sell me anything I didn't need. Points for that. I would more worried if a business (that's supposed to make money) didn't try to up sell stuff. Making money is the purpose of business, I'm more concerned with how they do it and these guys didn't over do it.

After the oil change my keys were left on top of the car out of my line of sight (this is just bad S.O.P) rather than handing me the keys and with modern cars the proximity keys are still detected out to a certain distance. So we drove off thinking the keys were in a cup holder in the dark and the key fob and keys ended up sliding off the car and getting run over.

The manager Lauren and all of the guys there at 8:30pm went out of their way to find busted up keys on foot and sent a mobile locksmith to meet me to program a new key. Now of course you would expect them to rectify a mistake. But they really went above and beyond to make things right and that is saying something. I've worked with other shops in the past and they could have just as easily given me the run around and/or tried to scam their way out of it. But these guys owned their mistake and made it right.

From my experience how well a shop works is one thing, but how they handle their mistakes speaks volumes. So while my overall experience wasn't the greatest given the problem with the keys, credit has to be given for how they handled the situation.<//review>

The Geffen has some interesting installations and artwork. It's part of the MOCA, so I was happy to see these two museums in a day for $15 usd (includes both). I think that's very reasonable for the amount of work you get to see. It's also nice to walk across town through Little Tokyo to get the other museum.

The Moca was a little less interesting. There was not as much to see. However, it's still worth the trip.</Review>

4< /rate>
<Text>Great exhibition space in Little Tokyo.  The galleries are larger in scale than the downtown location of MOCA, allowing for more diversity in the exhibitions.  No permanent collection at the Geffen, so check the website to see what's on view.  Exhibitions vary in quality and scope.  Note that a ticket bought at the Geffen will also get you into the downtown branch the same day, and vice versa.</Text>< pics>
None</pics>

<rate>5<//rate>< text>
Very interesting! If you buy a ticket to the MOCA dtla, it also gets you into this MOCA as well. It was a unique experience. It's very dark so wear flat shoes. The employees have flash lights for areas with steps but you should still walk slow. The exhibit itself was cool too! Definitely a must see!</text>

<rate>4< /rate><Text>It is a nice space, although smaller than I initially imagined, which is not always a bad thing. I found the space light, airy and manageable. There is a huge main room with a smaller offshoot room and a separate section if you cross the reception area. The staff are helpful and friendly and the collections interesting and varied.
Take time to sit outside and enjoy the sculpture and space, as well as visit the shop which is full of visual delights and easy to part with cash there.<//Text>< pictures>

<Rating>1<//Rating>< text>
For a museum that has a whole wall with the inscription "no more boring art", I feel you are falling short. A room with only a row of several suitcases. Another with a sawed-off tree that is bolted back together and supported with metal bracket, and yet another with a derelict aluminum wreck of a tracker in another room, leaves me wondering about no more boring art. Please!< /text>

<Date>1465258320481<//Date><rating>2< /rating>< review>
The idea of The Geffen sounded a lot better than it actually turned out to be with the described converted historic warehouse space. From the moment we entered the difficult to figure out entrance to be ignored by the staff who acted inconvenienced that we were trying to pay admission, we knew that we were not going to enjoy this museum. While some of the artwork was interesting and thought provoking, most tried too hard to be different and came across as either extremely sadistic or as boring as a library bookshelf. Next time I venture near Little Tokyo, the Geffen at MOCA won't be on my agenda.< /review>

113911152644428417162</user_id>
<response>None</response>< Gmap_id>
0x80c2c055e7b81dd3:0x1bc483918c98f83d<//Gmap_id>
<Pics>None< /Pics>< Text>
I went to MOCA this past Saturday for the Hello Kitty Convention it was extremely small venue for all the attendees.

I been a fan of Hello Kitty since my sister introduced me to her at a very young age with pencils, stationary, and pencil boxes you name it! Now, we are able to enjoy it with her girls at the Hello Kitty Con. I got us all tickets to attend the Hello Kitty Con and it was a great experience to share this with them and my other girlfriends and their daughters as well.

Let's get to the juicy details of the HK Con.

- I heard about the insane lines after lines through two elite yelpers and realized with kids going with us it's not a good idea to go early so we got there at 11am.
- We parked at a $6 parking structure off of Commerical & Alameda Ave. It was a far walk to MOCA but it wasn't too bad.
- To our surprise, there's still a long line to get in but it wasn't too bad.
- As we waited in line, the workers/staff were handing out pins, stickers, HK rings, and smiles =) everywhere.
- Although, the lines were super long, everyone was tolerable of the wait and was showing a lot of excitement.
- There were vendors/licensees that sold HK products in the Supermarket area.  I got a souvenir HK sweater and custom made shirt. Everything was pricey of course so you had to pick and choose what you wanted.
- I didn't bother with the shop upstairs since it was 3-4 hour wait and it reminded me of the shop at Puroland in Japan so why bother.
- Their were a lot of photo op everywhere and it was so fun to take so many pictures of the arts, decor, vintage HK stuff, and awesome back drops in every room!
- We were extremely disappointed in TARGET collaboration with HK in the Carnival Room. We waited about 2 hours to get in line and we were almost at front when they announced they were no longer letting people inside. The security guards didn't even communicated that the line was cut short and that they were no longer accepting people inside. The people inside took their time playing the games. I feel bad for our kids and other kids waiting to play games.
- Outside, they had a fake tattoo area, nail shop, caricature area, pumpkin patch, penny machine, arts & crafts, and a huge line for the shop.
- There ware food trucks outside with long lines. I think they should've had more food options. So, luckily we ate before going and were okay all day.
- My favorite was seeing Hello Kitty two times and Yuko Yamaguchi.  I missed out on all the freebies like free drawn picture, signing, and classes that were sold out.
- We stayed until 7pm even though they were closing until 9pm for HK Birthday. We missed our free opportunity to go to the Japanese Museum.

Overall, it was a enjoyable experience but I would complain about the venue being small, long lines, and the collaboration with Target being unorganized.

I'm glad my friends and I had a great time regardless. I know Sunday is madness. Good luck to the attendees on Sunday.<//Text>
